  \n  \n    Do not post: \n    \n  Threats that could lead to death (and other forms of high-severity violence) targeting people or places where threat is defined as any of the following:\n\n      \n              Statements of intent to commit high-severity violence. This includes content where a symbol represents the target and\/or includes a visual of an armament or method to represent violence. \n        Calls for high-severity violence including content where no target is specified but a symbol represents the target and\/or includes a visual of an armament or method that represents violence. \n        Statements advocating for high-severity violence. \n        Aspirational or conditional statements to commit high-severity violence. \n     \n      \n      Content that asks or offers services for hire to kill others (for example, hitmen, mercenaries, assassins) or advocates for the use of a hitman, mercenary or assassin against a target \n     \n      Admissions, statements of intent or advocacy, calls to action, or aspirational or conditional statements to kidnap a target \n      Content that depicts abductions or kidnappings if it is clear the content is not being shared by a victim or their family as a plea for help, or shared for informational, condemnation or awareness raising purposes \n\nThreats of high-severity violence using digitally-produced or altered imagery to target living people with armaments, methods of violence Facebook looks at the below signals to determine whether there is a threat of harm in the content.\n   \n     \n         Shared in a retaliatory context (e.g., expressions of desire to do something harmful to others in response to a grievance or threat that may be real, perceived or anticipated) \n References to historical or fictional incidents of violence (e.g., content that threatens others by referring to known historical incidents of violence that have been executed throughout history or in fictional settings) \n Acts as a threatening call-to-action (e.g. content inviting or encouraging others to carry out harmful acts or to join in carrying out the harmful acts) \n Indicates knowledge of or shares sensitive information that could expose others to harm (e.g. content that either makes note of or implies awareness of personal information that might make a threat of physical violence more credible. While we understand that people commonly express disdain or disagreement by threatening or calling for violence in non-serious ways, we remove language that incites or facilitates serious violence. We remove content, disable accounts and work with law enforcement when we believe there is a genuine risk of physical harm or direct threats to public safety. We also try to consider the language and context in order to distinguish casual statements from content that constitutes a credible threat to public or personal safety. In determining whether a threat is credible, we may also consider additional information like a person's public visibility and the risks to their physical safety. \n  \n     In some cases, we see aspirational or conditional threats directed at terrorists and other violent actors (e.g. \"Terrorists deserve to be killed\"), and we deem those non-credible, absent specific evidence to the contrary.  \n  \n "},"dangerous_individuals_organizations":{"other_content":"\n   \n  \n    We Remove: \n    \n      We remove Praise, Substantive Support, and Representation of various Dangerous Organizations. hate; or terrorism, including entities designated by the United States government as Foreign Terrorist Organizations (FTOs) or Specially Designated Global Terrorists (SDGTs), to have a presence onthe platform. We also don't allow other people to represent these entities. We do not allow leaders or prominent members of these organizations to have a presence on the platform, symbols that represent them to be used on the platform, or content that praises them or their acts. In addition, we remove any coordination of substantive support for these individuals and organizations. \n\n        We do not allow content that praises, substantively supports, or represents events that Facebook designates as terrorist attacks, hate events, mass murders or attempted mass murders, serial murders, hate crimes or violating violent events. \n\n We also do not allow Praise, Substantive Support, or Representation of designated hateful ideologies.\n \n       \n       \n            Terrorist organizations and individuals , defined as a non-state actor that: \n \n   Engages in, advocates, or lends substantial support to purposive and planned acts of violence, \n   Which causes or attempts to cause death, injury or serious harm to civilians, or any other person not taking direct part in the hostilities in a situation of armed conflict, and\/or significant damage to property linked to death, serious injury or serious harm to civilians \n   With the intent to coerce, intimidate and\/or influence a civilian population, government, or international organization \n   In order to achieve a political, religious, or ideological aim. \n\n         Hate Organizations , defined as an association of three or more people that: \n \n   is organized under a name, sign, or symbol; and  \n   has an ideology, statements, or physical actions that attack individuals based on characteristics, including race, religious affiliation, national origin, disability, ethnicity, gender, sex, sexual orientation, or serious disease. \n\n        Criminal Organizations , defined as an association of three or more people that: \n \n   is united under a name, color(s), hand gesture(s) or recognized indicia; and \n   has engaged in or threatens to engage in criminal activity such as homicide, drug trafficking, or kidnapping.  \n\n   Mass and Multiple Murderers  \n \n   We consider an event to be a mass murder or an attempted mass murder if it results in three or more casualties in one incident, defined as deaths or serious injuries. Any Individual who has committed such an attack is considered to be a mass murderer or an attempted mass murderer.  \n   We consider any individual who has committed two or more murders over multiple incidents or locations a multiple murderer. \n\n        \tHateful Ideologies \n \n   While our designations of organizations and individuals focus on behavior, we also recognize that there are certain ideologies and beliefs that are inherently tied to violence and attempts to organize people around calls for violence or exclusion of others based on their protected characteristics. In these cases, we designate the ideology itself and remove content that supports this ideology from our platform. These ideologies include:\n \n   Nazism \n   White Supremacy \n   White Nationalism \n   White Separatism \n   We remove explicit Praise, Substantive Support, and Representation of these ideologies, and remove individuals and organizations that ascribe to one or more of these hateful ideologies.  \n\n        Tier 2: Violent Non-State Actors \n\n        Organizations and individuals designated by Facebook as Violent Non-state Actors are not allowed to have a presence on Facebook, or have a presence maintained by others on their behalf. As these groups are actively engaged in violence, substantive support of these entities is similarly not allowed. We will also remove praise of violence carried out by these entities.  \n\n\n        Violent Non-State Actors , defined as any non-state actor that: \n \n   engages in purposive and planned acts of violence primarily against a government military or other armed groups; and \n        that causes or attempts to \n \n   cause death to persons taking direct part in hostilities in an armed conflict, and\/or \n   deprive communities of access to vital infrastructure and natural resources, and\/or bring significant damage to property, linked to death, serious injury or serious harm to civilians  \n\n\n\n        Tier 3: Militarized Social Movements, Violence-Inducing Conspiracy Networks, and Hate Banned Entities \n\n Pages, Groups, Events, and Profiles or other Facebook entities that are - or claim to be - maintained by, or on behalf of, Militarized Social Movements and Violence-Inducing Conspiracy Networks are prohibited. Admins of these pages, groups and events will also be removed. \n    Click here  to read more about how we address movements and organizations tied to violence. \n   We do not allow Representation of Organizations and individuals designated by Facebook as Hate-Banned Entities.  \n\n\n        Militarized Social Movements (MSMs) , which include: \n \n \n   Militia Groups , defined as non-state actors that use weapons as a part of their training, communication, or presence; or \n   Arson, Looting, or other destruction of property; or \n   Threaten to violently disrupt an election process; or \n   Promote bringing weapons to a location when the stated intent is to intimidate people amid a protest. \n \n   Violence-Inducing Conspiracy Networks (VICNs) , defined as a Non-State Actor that:\n \n   Organizes under a name, sign, mission statement, or symbol; and \n   Promote theories that attribute violent or dehumanizing behavior to people or organizations that have been debunked by credible sources; and \n   Has inspired multiple incidents of real-world violence by adherents motivated by the desire to draw attention to or redress the supposed harms promoted by these debunked theories.  \n\n        Hate-Banned Entities , defined as entities that engage in repeated hateful conduct or rhetoric, but do not rise to the level of a Tier 1 entity because they have not engaged in or explicitly advocated for violence, or because they lack sufficient connections to previously designated organizations or figures.  \n   \n       \n       \n       \n       \n   \n   \n ","policy_rationale":"\n\n   \n\n     In an effort to prevent and disrupt real-world harm, we do not allow organizations or individuals that proclaim a violent mission or are engaged in violence to have a presence on Facebook. We assess these entities based on their behavior both online and offline, most significantly, their ties to violence. Under this policy, we designate individuals, organizations, and networks of people. These designations are divided into three tiers that indicate the level of content enforcement, with Tier 1 resulting in the most extensive enforcement because we believe these entities have the most direct ties to offline harm. \n\n     Tier 1  focuses on entities that engage in serious offline harms - including organizing or advocating for violence against civilians, repeatedly dehumanizing or advocating for harm against people based on protected characteristics, or engaging in systematic criminal operations. Tier 1 entities include terrorist, hate, and criminal organizations.   We remove praise, substantive support, and representation of Tier 1 entities as well as their leaders, founders, or prominent members. Tier 1 includes hate organizations; criminal organizations, including those designated by the United States government as Specially Designated Narcotics Trafficking Kingpins (SDNTKs); and terrorist organizations, including entities and individuals designated by the United States government as Foreign Terrorist Organizations (FTOs) or Specially Designated Global Terrorists (SDGTs).  We remove praise, substantive support, and representation of Tier 1 entities as well as their leaders, founders, or prominent members.  \n\n     In addition, we do not allow content that praises, substantively supports, or represents events that Facebook designates as violating violent events - including terrorist attacks, hate events, mass murders or attempted mass murders, multiple murders, or hate crimes. Nor do we allow praise, substantive support, or representation of the perpetrator(s) of such attacks. We also remove content that praises, substantively supports or represents ideologies that promote hate, such as nazism and white supremacy. \n\n     Tier 2  focuses on entities that engage in violence against state or military actors but do not generally target civilians -- what we call \u201cViolent Non-State Actors.\u201d  We remove all substantive support and representation of these entities, their leaders, and their prominent members. We remove any praise of these groups\u2019 violent activities. \n\n     Tier 3  focuses on entities that may repeatedly engage in violations of our Hate Speech or Dangerous Organizations policies on-or-off the platform or demonstrate strong intent to engage in offline violence in the near future, but have not necessarily engaged in violence to date or advocated for violence against others based on their protected characteristics. This includes Militarized Social Movements, Violence-Inducing Conspiracy Networks, and individuals and groups banned for promoting hatred. Tier 3 entities may not have a presence or coordinate on our platforms.  \n\n     We recognize that users may share content that includes references to designated dangerous organizations and individuals to report on, condemn, or neutrally discuss them or their activities. Our policies are designed to allow room for these types of discussions, but we require people to clearly indicate their intent. If the intention is unclear, we may remove content. \n\n\n  \n "},"coordinating_harm_publicizing_crime":{"other_content":"\n   \n \n  \n    Do not post content that falls into the following We also prohibit the purchase, sale, gifting, exchange, and transfer of firearms, including firearm parts or ammunition, between private individuals on Facebook. Some of these items are not regulated everywhere; however, because of the borderless nature of our community, we try to enforce our policies as consistently as possible. Firearm stores and online retailers may promote items available for sale off of our services as long as those retailers comply with all applicable laws and regulations. We allow discussions about sales of firearms and firearm parts in stores or by online retailers and advocating for changes to firearm regulation.    \n     \n     We may remove suicide notes when we have confirmation of a suicide or suicide attempt. We try to identify suicide notes using several factors, including but not limited to, family or legal representative requests, media reports, law enforcement reports or other third party sources (e.g. government agencies, NGOs).\n     \n       A suicide note may also be removed when reported through the   Suicidal Content Contact Form   or  Instagram Contact Form  when we have confirmation of a suicide or suicide attempt \n       \n    \n  \n ","policy_rationale":"\n   We care deeply about the safety of the people who use our apps. We regularly consult with experts in suicide and self-injury to help inform our policies and enforcement, and work with organizations around the world to provide assistance to people in distress.\n     \nWhile we do not allow people to intentionally or unintentionally celebrate or promote suicide or self-injury, we do allow people to discuss these topics because we want Facebook to be a space where people can share their experiences, raise awareness about these issues, and seek support from one another.\n  \nWe define self-injury as the intentional and direct injuring of the body, including self-mutilation and eating disorders. We remove any content that encourages suicide or self-injury, including fictional content such as memes or illustrations and any self-injury content which is graphic, regardless of context. We also remove content that identifies and negatively targets victims or survivors of suicide or self-injury seriously, humorously or rhetorically, as well as real time depictions of suicide or self-injury. Content about recovery of suicide or self-harm that is allowed, but may contain imagery that could be upsetting, such as a healed scar, is placed behind a sensitivity screen.\n  \nWhen people post or search for suicide or self-injury- related content, we will direct them to local organizations that can provide support and if someone is at immediate risk of harming themselves, we will contact local emergency services to get them help.\n  \nWith respect to live content, experts have told us that if someone is saying they intend to attempt suicide on a livestream, we should leave the content up for as long as possible, because the longer someone is talking to a camera, the more opportunity there is for a friend or family member to call emergency services.\n  \nHowever, to minimize the risk of others being negatively impacted by viewing this content, we will stop the livestream at the point at which the threat turns into an attempt. As mentioned above, in any case, we will contact emergency services if we identify someone is at immediate risk of harming themselves.\n  \n     \n \n otherwise deemed to be objectionable in local context  \n   \n  \n   \n   \n   \n   \n   \n \n  \n  \n ","policy_rationale":"\n   Bullying and harassment happen in many places and come in many different forms from making threats and releasing personally identifiable information to sending threatening messages and making unwanted malicious contact. We do not tolerate this kind of behavior because it prevents people from feeling safe and respected on Facebook.  \n\n We distinguish between public figures and private individuals because we want to allow discussion, which often includes critical commentary of people who are featured in the news or who have a large public audience. For public figures, we remove attacks that are severe as well as certain attacks where the public figure is directly tagged in the post or comment.  \n  \n   For private individuals, our protection goes further: We remove content that's meant to degrade or shame, including, for example, claims about someone's sexual personal activity. We recognize that bullying and harassment can have more of an emotional impact on minors, which is why our policies provide heightened protection for users between the ages of 13 and 18. \n\n Context and intent matter, and we allow people to post and share if it is clear that something was shared in order to condemn or draw attention to bullying and harassment. In certain instances, we require self-reporting because it helps us understand that the person targeted feels bullied or harassed. In addition to reporting such behavior and content, we encourage people to use  tools available on Facebook  to help protect against it. \n    \n     We also have a  Bullying Prevention Hub , which is a resource for teens, parents, and educators seeking support for issues related to bullying and other conflicts. It offers step-by-step guidance, including information on how to start important conversations about bullying. Learn more about what we are doing to protect people from bullying and harassment  here . \n     Note: This policy does not apply to individuals who are part of designated organizations under the  Dangerous Organizations and Individuals policy  or individuals who died prior to 1900. \n   \n "},"human_exploitation":{"other_content":"\n   \n  \n    Do not post: \n    \n      Content or exhibited behavior that may lead to human exploitation, which includes any of the following:\n\n      \n        Sex trafficking, covering minors and adults. \n        The sale of children for illegal adoption.\n         \n        Orphanage trafficking and orphanage volun-tourism.\n           \n        Forced marriages.\n         \n        Labor exploitation (including bonded labor).\n         \n        Domestic servitude.\n         \n        Non-regenerative organ trafficking. \n        Forced criminal activity (e.g. forced begging, forced drug trafficking). \n        Recruitment of child soldiers. \n           \n\n      Content geared towards the:\n      \n        Recruitment of potential victims through force, fraud, coercion, enticement, deception, blackmail or other non-consensual acts. \n        Facilitation of human exploitation by coordinating, transporting, transferring, harboring or brokering of victims prior or during the exploitation.  \n        Exploitation of humans by promoting, depicting or advocating for it. \n        \n      Content that offers to provide or facilitate human smuggling \n      \n         \n    \n ","policy_rationale":"\n   After consulting with outside experts from around the world, we are consolidating several existing exploitation policies, that were previously housed in different sections of the Community Standards into one dedicated section that focuses on human exploitation and captures a broad range of harmful activities that may manifest on our platform. Experts think and talk about these issues under one umbrella human exploitation.   \n     \n     \n     \n      In an effort to disrupt and prevent harm, we remove content that facilitates or coordinates the exploitation of humans, including human trafficking. We define human trafficking as the business of depriving someone of liberty for profit. It is the exploitation of humans in order to force them to engage   in commercial sex, labor or other activities against their will. It relies on deception, force and coercion, and degrades humans by depriving them of their freedom while economically or materially benefiting others.   \n     \n     \n     \n      Human trafficking is multi-faceted and global; it can affect anyone regardless of age, socioeconomic background, ethnicity, gender or location. It takes many forms, and any given trafficking situation can involve various stages of development. By the coercive nature of this abuse, victims cannot consent. \n     \n     \n     \n      While we need to be careful not to conflate human trafficking and smuggling, they can be related and exhibit overlap. The United Nations defines human smuggling as the procurement or facilitation of illegal entry into a state across international borders. Without necessity for coercion or force, it may still result in the exploitation of vulnerable individuals who are trying to leave their country of origin, often in pursuit of a better life. Human smuggling is a crime against a state, relying on movement, and human trafficking is a crime against a person, relying on exploitation. \n \n Facebook looks at a range of signs to determine whether there is a threat of harm in the content. These include but are not limited to: content that could incite imminent violence or intimidation; whether there is a period of heightened  tension such as an election or ongoing conflict; and whether there is a recent history of violence against the targeted protected group. In some cases, we may also consider whether the speaker is a public figure or occupies a position of authority.  \n     \n      \n   \n  \n ","policy_rationale":"\n   We believe that people use their voice and connect more freely when they don\u2019t feel attacked on the basis of who they are. That is why we don\u2019t allow hate speech on Facebook. It creates an environment of intimidation and exclusion, and in some cases may promote offline violence. \n\n     We define hate speech as a direct attack against people \u2014 rather than concepts or institutions\u2014 on the basis of what we call protected characteristics: race, ethnicity, national origin, disability, religious affiliation, caste, sexual orientation, sex, gender identity and serious disease. We define attacks as violent or dehumanizing speech, harmful stereotypes, statements of inferiority, expressions of contempt, disgust or dismissal, cursing and calls for exclusion or segregation. We also prohibit the use of harmful stereotypes, which we define as dehumanizing comparisons that have historically been used to attack, intimidate, or exclude specific groups, and that are often linked with offline violence.  We consider age a protected characteristic when referenced along with another protected characteristic. We also protect refugees, migrants, immigrants and asylum seekers from the most severe attacks, though we do allow commentary and criticism of immigration policies. Similarly, we provide some protections for characteristics like occupation, when they\u2019re referenced along with a protected characteristic. \n    \n    \n     We recognize that people sometimes share content that includes someone else\u2019s hate speech to condemn it or raise awareness. In other cases, speech that might otherwise violate our standards can be used self-referentially or in an empowering way. Our policies are designed to allow room for these types of speech, but we require people to clearly indicate their intent. If the intention is unclear, we may remove content. \n    \n\n     Learn more about our approach to hate speech.\n   \n \n "},"graphic_violence":{"other_content":"\n   \n  \n    Do not post: \n    \n      Imagery of people   \n Videos of people or dead bodies in non-medical settings if they depict\n   \n  \t Dismemberment. \n     Visible internal organs; partially decomposed bodies. \n     Charred or burning people unless in the context of cremation or self-immolation when that action is a form of political speech or newsworthy. \n     Victims of cannibalism. \n     Throat-slitting. \n        \n \n      Live streams of capital punishment of a person \n\n     \n    \n  \n   \n      \n  For the following content, we include a warning screen so that people are aware the content may be disturbing. We believe that authenticity helps create a community where people are accountable to each other, and to Facebook, in meaningful ways. We want to allow for the range of diverse ways that identity is expressed across our global community, while also preventing impersonation and identity misrepresentation. That is why we require people to connect on Facebook using the name they go by in everyday life. Our authenticity policies are intended to create a safe environment where people can trust and hold one another accountable.\n     \n  In order to maintain a safe environment and empower free expression, we remove accounts that are harmful to the community, including those that compromise the security of other accounts and our services. We have built a combination of automated and manual systems to block and remove accounts that are used to persistently or egregiously abuse our Community Standards.  \n  \n    Because account level removal is a severe action, whenever possible, we aim to give our community a chance to learn our rules and follow our Community Standards.  Penalties, including account disables, are designed to be proportionate to the severity of the violation and the risk of harm posed to the community. Continued violations, despite repeated warnings and restrictions, or violations that pose severe safety risks will lead to an account being disabled.   \n "},"spam":{"other_content":"\n   \n  \n    Do not: \n    \n \n   Post, share, engage with content or create accounts, Groups, Pages, Events or other assets, either manually or automatically, at very high frequencies. \n   Attempt to or successfully sell, buy or exchange site privileges or product features, such as accounts, admin roles, permission to post, Pages, Groups, likes, etc., except in the case of clearly identified branded content, as defined by our  Branded Content Policies .\n   \n   \n     Require or claim that users are required to engage with content (e.g. liking, sharing) before they are able to view or interact with promised content.    \n     Encourage likes, shares, follows, clicks or the use of apps or websites under false pretenses, such as:\n  \t \n       Offering false or non-existent services or functionality(e.g. \u201cGet a \u2018Dislike\u2019 button!\u201d) \n       Failing to direct to promised content (e.g. \u201cClick here for a discount code at Nordstrom\u201d;  false play buttons ) \n       Directing users off of Facebook through the deceptive or misleading use of URLs, defined as:\n         \n           Cloaking. We are a service for more than two billion people to freely express themselves across countries and cultures and in dozens of languages. \n     We recognize how important it is for Facebook to be a place where people feel empowered to communicate, and we take seriously our role in keeping abuse off our service. That\u2019s why we\u2019ve  developed a set of Community Standards  that outline what is and is not allowed on Facebook. Our policies are based on feedback from our community and the advice of experts in fields such as technology, public safety and human rights. To ensure that everyone\u2019s voice is valued, we take great care to craft policies that are inclusive of different views and beliefs, in particular those of people and communities that might otherwise be overlooked or marginalized. \n     Please note that the US English version of the Community Standards reflects the most up to date set of the policies and should be used as the master document. \n   \n         \n     REITERATING OUR COMMITMENT TO VOICE \n     The goal of our Community Standards has always been to  create a place for expression and give people a voice . This has not and will not change. Building community and bringing the world closer together depends on people\u2019s ability to share diverse views, experiences, ideas and information. We want people to be able to talk openly about the issues that matter to them, even if some may disagree or find them objectionable. In some cases, we allow content for public awareness which would otherwise go against our Community Standards \u2013 if it is newsworthy and in the public interest. We do this only after weighing the public interest value against the risk of harm and we look to international human rights standards,  as reflected in our Corporate Human Rights Policy,   to make these judgments. As such, we consider the newsworthiness of content posted by anyone, including news organizations and individuals users. For example, we have allowed content that graphically depicts war or the consequences of war where it is important to public discourse.  \n    \n     Our commitment to expression is paramount, but we recognize the internet creates new and increased opportunities for abuse. For these reasons, when we limit expression, we do it in service of one or more of the following values: \n   \n       \n\n     Authenticity:  We want to make sure the content people are seeing on Facebook is authentic. We believe that authenticity creates a better environment for sharing, and that\u2019s why we don\u2019t want people using Facebook to misrepresent who they are or what they\u2019re doing.\n \n    \n    \n      \n    \n     Safety:  We are committed to making Facebook a safe place. Expression that threatens people has the potential to intimidate, exclude or silence others and isn\u2019t allowed on Facebook. \n  \n    \n  \n    \n    \n     Privacy:  We are committed to protecting personal privacy and information. Privacy gives people the freedom to be themselves, and to choose how and when to share on Facebook and to connect more easily.\n \n        \n  \n    \n     Dignity:  We believe that all people are equal in dignity and rights. We expect that people will respect the dignity of others and not harass or degrade others. \n    \n\n\n    \n    \n     Our Community Standards apply to everyone, all around the world, and to all types of content. They\u2019re designed to be comprehensive \u2013 for example, content that might not be considered hateful may still be removed for violating a different policy. We recognize that words mean different things or affect people differently depending on their local community, language, or background. We work hard to account for these nuances while also applying our policies consistently and fairly to people and their expression. Our enforcement of these standards relies on information available to us. In some cases, this means that we may not detect content and behavior that violates these standards, and in others,  enforcement may be limited to circumstances where we have been provided with additional information and context. \n\n     People can report potentially violating content, including Pages, Groups, Profiles, individual content, and comments. We also give people control over their own experience by allowing them to\n       block ,   unfollow \n       or \n        hide  people and posts.\n       \n\n     The consequences for violating our Community Standards vary depending on the severity of the violation and the person's history on the platform. For instance, we may warn someone for a first violation, but if they continue to violate our policies, we may restrict their ability to post on Facebook or disable their profile. We also may notify law enforcement when we believe there is a genuine risk of physical harm or a direct threat to public safety. \n     Our Community Standards are a guide for what is and isn\u2019t allowed on Facebook. style="display:block;height:0;overflow:hidden;position:absolute;width:0;padding:0">Facebook</h1><div id="page"><div class="_129_" id="header-notices"><div class="_du6 chrome windows" id="u_0_3_Ml"><div class="_7om2 _du7"><div class="_4g34"><div class="_dui"></div></div><div class="_4g34 _duc"><div><header class="_du8"><h2>Selainta ei tueta</h2></header><article>Facebook ei tue kyttmsi selainta. Olemme ohjanneet sinut uudelleen yksinkertaisempaan versioon, joka tarjoaa hyvn kyttkokemuksen.</article></div></div></div></div></div><div class="_59e9" id="root" role="main" data-sigil="context-layer-root content-pane"><div class="_7om2 _4ft8"><div class="_4g34"><!-- begin-react-placeholder --><div><div class="_6uwf _6_gw _89ag"><div class="_6uwi"><div class="_6uwk"><div class="_6_ht"><a href="/communitystandards/?privacy_mutation_token=eyJ0eXBlIjowLCJjcmVhdGlvbl90aW1lIjoxNjMwOTg5MDQ4LCJjYWxsc2l0ZV9pZCI6MzQ5NzUyNzQyNzYwNjEwfQ%3D%3D"><i class="img sp_eS0Fnf3fNg2 sx_12983c"></i></a></div><div class="_89af">Yhteisnormit</div></div></div></div><div class="_76ea"></div></div><!-- end-react-placeholder --><noscript id="u_0_0_il"></noscript><div id="u_0_1_FX"><noscript id="u_0_2_0s"></noscript><div class="_11u6"><a href="/communitystandards/?video"><i class="img img _2sxw _4s0y" style="background-image: url(&#039;https\3a //static.xx.fbcdn.net/rsrc.php/v3/yr/r/WhZnYf_tjgg.png&#039;);background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:100% 100%;-webkit-background-size:100% 100%;padding-bottom:56.25%;"></i></a></div><div class="_12bc _11wv"><div><div class="_297a"><div class="_21c0"><div class="_21c1">JOHDANTO</div><div class="_4n96"><p class="_3i--">Ihmiset kyttvt Facebookia pivittin jakaakseen kokemuksiaan, muodostaakseen yhteyksi ystviins ja perheenjseniins ja rakentaakseen yhteisj. Yli kaksi miljardia ihmist kytt palveluamme ilmaistakseen itsen vapaasti kymmenill eri kielill maiden ja kulttuurien rajat ylitten.</p><p class="_3i--">Ymmrrmme ehdottomasti, ett Facebookin tytyy olla paikka, jossa ihmiset tuntevat itsens voimaantuneiksi ja kokevat kykenevns viestimn vapaasti. Siksi suhtaudumme vrinkytsten kitkemiseen palvelustamme erittin vakavasti. Tmn vuoksi olemme <a href="https://lm.facebook.com/l.php?u=https%3A%2F%2Fnewsroom.fb.com%2Fnews%2F2019%2F04%2Finsidefeed-community-standards-development-process%2F&amp;h=AT0o5VVZ0QqZi6CYvwR730jQ3xexzwr7y3cOjz7N24t4zUhigOragt5JHT4O_rZm10FIna8OnhJYC9tSCRvPtisPrUVCFgmj2qdtPGBo-3lC6t56CqxLs820JZWlID2LmDkR1TBY2pBSk8oXKyCQ" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" data-lynx-mode="asynclazy">kehittneet yhteisnormit</a>, joissa mritetn, mik on sallittua ja kielletty Facebookissa. Kytntmme perustuvat palautteeseen, jonka olemme saaneet yhteisltmme ja teknologian, yleisen turvallisuuden, ihmisoikeuksien ja muiden alojen asiantuntijoilta. Varmistaaksemme, ett jokaisen nt arvostetaan, luomme huolellisesti kytntj, jotka hyvksyvt kaikki nkemykset ja uskomukset, etenkin niilt ihmisilt ja yhteisilt, joita saatettaisiin muuten ylenkatsoa, vheksy tai marginalisoida.</p><div style="text-align: center"><i class="img _257 _4cef img _2sxw" style="background-image: url(&#039;https\3a //scontent-arn2-2.xx.fbcdn.net/v/t39.2365-6/30179729_1969747913355382_7724706176021037056_n.png?_nc_cat\3d 1\26 ccb\3d 1-5\26 _nc_sid\3d ad8a9d\26 _nc_ohc\3d li5L3o3Y8gAAX8dctgZ\26 _nc_ht\3d scontent-arn2-2.xx\26 oh\3d 0c802fa51b587df99a65f48dfea09fe2\26 oe\3d 613CD1BA&#039;);background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:100% 100%;-webkit-background-size:100% 100%;width:166px;height:163px;"></i></div><br /><div class="_21c1">TOISTAMME SITOUTUMISEMME NEN ANTAMISEEN</div><p class="_3i--">Yhteisnormiemme pmrn on aina ollut <a href="https://lm.facebook.com/l.php?u=https%3A%2F%2Fnewsroom.fb.com%2Fnews%2F2018%2F08%2Fhard-questions-free-expression%2F&amp;h=AT261wB8HJ_8Xm0wP7NTtPgLYGm_FtdNCflMASw0lVZdFZWCFA_gZAZxZWTYvBHQajmq5NXcrFRYNPyZukm2rBhrSCxPkDsVO30NfcVRTmt66Q6hcfjkX7ayHuNgeEA35TwB8_d75-HMCppD0nw6" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" data-lynx-mode="asynclazy">luoda paikka ilmaisulle ja antaa ihmisille ni</a>. Tm ei ole muuttunut eik tule muuttumaan. Yhteisn rakentaminen ja maailman ihmisten tuominen toisiaan lhemmksi riippuu ihmisten kyvyst jakaa erilaisia nkemyksi, kokemuksia, ideoita ja tietoa. Haluamme, ett ihmisill on mahdollisuus puhua avoimesti asioista, joilla on heille merkityst, vaikka jotkut eivt olisi niist samaa mielt tai vastustaisivat niit. Joissakin tapauksissa sallimme sislln, joka olisi muutoin yhteisnormiemme vastaista, jos sill on yleishydyllist arvoa ja uutisarvoa. Teemme niin vasta punnittuamme sislln yleishydyllisen arvon suhteessa sen mahdollisesti aiheuttamien vahinkojen vaaraan. Teemme nm ptkset <a href="https://lm.facebook.com/l.php?u=https%3A%2F%2Fabout.fb.com%2Fwp-content%2Fuploads%2F2021%2F03%2FFacebooks-Corporate-Human-Rights-Policy.pdf&amp;h=AT2sQt6h91zJ0GRRZaBtQ9YvL1YChg9K67_Tatm8dG_7P0RQ10vuAK86wS7QL9JKcLSvbjoeYSNPqEEb7Pqr-l5OBD9EfbkCXjvlWzP2YWsWZ2uYj3XBPEiIe49iLnT6xr5nrLPu7ULpMsPXt6zc" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" data-lynx-mode="asynclazy">yhtin ihmisoikeuskytnnss</a> tarkoitettujen kansainvlisten ihmisoikeusstandardien perusteella. Pohdimme sislln uutisarvoa niin uutisorganisaatioiden kuin yksityistenkin kyttjien julkaisujen kohdalla. Sallimme esimerkiksi sislln, joka sislt jrkyttvi kuvia sodasta tai sodan seurauksista, jos se on trke julkisen keskustelun kannalta.</p><p class="_3i--">Sitoutumisemme ilmaisuun on trkeydessn ensisijainen, mutta ymmrrmme, ett internet luo jatkuvasti ja eneneviss mrin uusia mahdollisuuksia vrinkytksiin. Tst johtuen rajoitamme ilmaisua silloin, kun pyrimme noudattamaan yht tai useampaa seuraavista arvoista:</p><br /><div style="text-align: center"><i class="img _257 _4cef img _2sxw" style="background-image: url(&#039;https\3a //scontent-arn2-2.xx.fbcdn.net/v/t39.2365-6/70546071_460725341450782_7389006442629431296_n.png?_nc_cat\3d 1\26 ccb\3d 1-5\26 _nc_sid\3d ad8a9d\26 _nc_ohc\3d xoR5VbBgrNoAX9OKkvg\26 _nc_ht\3d scontent-arn2-2.xx\26 oh\3d 61a4fa718a6f4dc664fcb423354ecc77\26 oe\3d 613BE3A5&#039;);background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:100% 100%;-webkit-background-size:100% 100%;width:172px;height:162px;"></i></div><p class="_3i--"><b>Aitous ja todenmukaisuus:</b> Haluamme varmistaa, ett ihmiset nkevt Facebookissa aitoa ja todenmukaista sislt. Uskomme, ett aitous ja todenmukaisuus luovat paremman ympristn jakamiselle, mink vuoksi emme halua, ett ihmiset kyttvt Facebookia antaakseen itsestn tai tekemisistn vrn tai harhaanjohtavan kuvan. </p><div style="text-align: center"><i class="img _257 _4cef img _2sxw" style="background-image: url(&#039;https\3a //scontent-arn2-2.xx.fbcdn.net/v/t39.2365-6/30179798_233411330550983_830803110640222208_n.png?_nc_cat\3d 1\26 ccb\3d 1-5\26 _nc_sid\3d ad8a9d\26 _nc_ohc\3d ecTD6my_eS4AX_1kgjO\26 _nc_ht\3d scontent-arn2-2.xx\26 oh\3d 678822453f17b01fc907e229595075fc\26 oe\3d 613B0AE3&#039;);background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:100% 100%;-webkit-background-size:100% 100%;width:166px;height:163px;"></i></div><p class="_3i--"><b>Turvallisuus:</b> Olemme sitoutuneet tekemn Facebookista turvallisen paikan. Ihmisi uhkaavat ilmaisun muodot voivat pelotella, syrji tai hiljent muita, eik niit sallita Facebookissa.</p><br /><div style="text-align: center"><i class="img _257 _4cef img _2sxw" style="background-image: url(&#039;https\3a //scontent-arn2-2.xx.fbcdn.net/v/t39.2365-6/70744027_1120870694776290_6189555203662938112_n.png?_nc_cat\3d 1\26 ccb\3d 1-5\26 _nc_sid\3d ad8a9d\26 _nc_ohc\3d ry-rjx_zQ2sAX91O5yQ\26 _nc_ht\3d scontent-arn2-2.xx\26 oh\3d 141647bc2922b1ccba367edcbe8d92a7\26 oe\3d 613BEA50&#039;);background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:100% 100%;-webkit-background-size:100% 100%;width:172px;height:162px;"></i></div><p class="_3i--"><b>Yksityisyys:</b> Olemme sitoutuneet suojaamaan henkilkohtaista yksityisyytt ja tietoja. Yksityisyys antaa ihmisille vapauden olla oma itsens ja valita miten ja koska jakaa Facebookissa. Sen ansiosta ihmiset voivat mys muodostaa helpommin yhteyksi toisiinsa. </p><div style="text-align: center"><i class="img _257 _4cef img _2sxw" style="background-image: url(&#039;https\3a //scontent-arn2-2.xx.fbcdn.net/v/t39.2365-6/70707979_539090683561979_6815354865225564160_n.png?_nc_cat\3d 1\26 ccb\3d 1-5\26 _nc_sid\3d ad8a9d\26 _nc_ohc\3d vZoUjm0qUI0AX-xFzqp\26 _nc_ht\3d scontent-arn2-2.xx\26 oh\3d 20935c3a3c920e2882521c8aadfb90df\26 oe\3d 613B5D82&#039;);background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:100% 100%;-webkit-background-size:100% 100%;width:159px;height:167px;"></i></div><p class="_3i--"><b>Arvokkuus:</b> Uskomme, ett kaikki ihmiset ovat tasa-arvoisia ja ett kaikille kuuluvat samat oikeudet. Odotamme, ett ihmiset kunnioittavat toisten tasa-arvoista asemaa eivtk hiritse tai halvenna toisia.</p><p class="_3i--">Yhteisnormimme koskevat maailmanlaajuisesti kaikkia ihmisi ja kaikenlaista sislt. Normit on suunniteltu kokonaisvaltaisen kattaviksi. Esimerkiksi sislt, jota ei ehk katsota eptoivotulla tavalla vihaiseksi, saatetaan silti poistaa toisen kytnnn rikkomisen vuoksi. Ymmrrmme, ett sanojen merkitys ja vaikutus ihmisiin vaihtelee paikallisyhteisst, kielest tai taustasta riippuen. Tyskentelemme jatkuvasti ottaaksemme nm svyerot ja vaihtelut huomioon samalla, kun kytmme kytntjmme johdonmukaisesti ja oikeudenmukaisesti ihmisten ja heidn ilmaisunsa yhteydess. Niden kytntjen tytntnpano perustuu saatavilla oleviin tietoihin. Tm tarkoittaa sit, ett emme vlttmtt pysty aina havaitsemaan sislt tai toimintaa, joka rikkoo nit kytntj, ja joissakin tapauksissa <a href="https://lm.facebook.com/l.php?u=https%3A%2F%2Fabout.fb.com%2Fnews%2F2020%2F11%2Fcommunity-standards-enforcement-report-nov-2020%2F&amp;h=AT3WNTkTQDnegXEdBXEyKmJSPuo2RmvUumCafWcbjCm-tC0E3fCuAe6sx4W2GhCeaX5G-uaCvCV8EB9EdgGkDpFjnhZRps8Da7D1gSFf49nnkMNfxUedGgRR7LMdfQRM1AWa6cqPzBnO6uzdltFV" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" data-lynx-mode="asynclazy">tytntnpano edellytt listietojen ja -kontekstin toimittamista.</a></p><p class="_3i--">Kyttjt voivat ilmiantaa sislt, joka saattaa rikkoa normeja, kuten sivuja, ryhmi, profiileja, yksittisi sisltj ja kommentteja. Annamme ihmisten hallita mys omaa kyttkokemustaan: he voivat<a href="https://www.facebook.com/help/168009843260943?ref=ccs">est</a> tai <a href="https://www.facebook.com/help/268028706671439?ref=ccs">piilottaa</a> ihmisi ja julkaisuja tai <a href="https://www.facebook.com/help/276458109035418?ref=ccs">lopettaa seuraamisen</a>. </p><p class="_3i--">Yhteisnormiemme rikkomisen seuraamukset riippuvat rikkeen vakavuudesta ja siit, onko ilmiannetun sislln julkaissut henkil rikkonut alustan kytntj aiemmin. Saatamme esimerkiksi antaa ensimmisest rikkomuksesta varoituksen, mutta rikkeiden jatkuessa voimme rajoittaa henkiln julkaisemista Facebookissa tai poistaa hnen profiilinsa kytst kokonaan. Saatamme mys ilmoittaa viranomaisille, kun uskomme olemassa olevan todellisen fyysisen vahingonteon riskin tai suoria uhkia yleiselle turvallisuudelle.</p><p class="_3i--">Yhteisnormimme ovat opas sille, mik Facebookissa on sallittua ja mik ei. Siksi pyydmmekin kaikkia Facebook-yhteisn jseni noudattamaan niit.</p><p class="_3i--"><b>Huomioithan, ett yhteisnormien englanninkielinen versio edustaa kytntj ajankohtaisimmin ja sit tulisi kytt pasiallisena asiakirjana.</b></p></div></div></div></div><div class="_2kpl"><div class="_2wqn"><div class="_68lm"><a
